sitedir-ltr mw-hide-empty-elt ns-0 ns-subject page-Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award rootpage-Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award skin-vector action-view">\t\t<div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n<div id="mw-indicator-featured-star" class="mw-indicator"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_lists" title="This is a featured list. Click here for more information."><img alt="This is a featured list. Click here for more information." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/20px-Cscr-featured.svg.png" width="20" height="19" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/30px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/40px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #AAD0FF;">Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award (MVP)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg" class="image" title="A black circle with an octagonal silver plaque in the middle. The edge of the plaque reads &quot;KENESAW MOUNTAIN LANDIS MEMORIAL BASEBALL AWARD&quot;. In the middle of the octagon is a baseball diamond which contains, from the top, Judge Landis&#39; face in gold, &quot;Most Valuable Player&quot;, the winner&#39;s league, his name in a gold rectangle, and his team."><img alt="A black circle with an octagonal silver plaque in the middle. The edge of the plaque reads &quot;KENESAW MOUNTAIN LANDIS MEMORIAL BASEBALL AWARD&quot;. In the middle of the octagon is a baseball diamond which contains, from the top, Judge Landis&#39; face in gold, &quot;Most Valuable Player&quot;, the winner&#39;s league, his name in a gold rectangle, and his team." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg/220px-National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg" width="220" height="228" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg/330px-National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg/440px-National-league-most-valuable-player-award_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="896" /></a><div>The Most Valuable Player award</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Given for</th><td>\nMajor League Baseball\'s Regular Season MVP</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Country</th><td>\nUnited States</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Presented by</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Baseball_Writers%27_Association_of_America" title="Baseball Writers&#39; Association of America">Baseball Writers\' Association of America</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #AAD0FF;">History</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">First award</th><td>\n1931</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Most recent</th><td>\n<div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Altuve" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Altuve">Jos\xc3\xa9 Altuve</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Giancarlo_Stanton" title="Giancarlo Stanton">Giancarlo Stanton</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award</b> (<b>MVP</b>) is an annual <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) award given to one outstanding player in the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> and one in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>. Since 1931, it has been awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Writers%27_Association_of_America" title="Baseball Writers&#39; Association of America">Baseball Writers\' Association of America</a> (BBWAA). The winners receive the <a href="/wiki/Kenesaw_Mountain_Landis" title="Kenesaw Mountain Landis">Kenesaw Mountain Landis</a> Memorial Baseball Award, which became the official name of the award in 1944,<sup id="cite_ref-LandisNBHoF_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LandisNBHoF-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> in honor of the first <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball_(MLB)" class="mw-redirect" title="Commissioner of Baseball (MLB)">MLB commissioner</a>, Kenesaw Mountain Landis, who served from 1920 until his death on November 25, 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-LandisNBHoF_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LandisNBHoF-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_1763_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN_1763-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>MVP voting takes place before the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason" title="Major League Baseball postseason">postseason</a>, but the results are not announced until after the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>. The BBWAA began by polling three writers in each league city in 1938, reducing that number to two per league city in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The BBWAA does not offer a clear-cut definition of what "most valuable" means, instead leaving the judgment to the individual voters.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/First_basemen" class="mw-redirect" title="First basemen">First basemen</a>, with 34&#160;winners, have won the most MVPs among <a href="/wiki/Infielder" title="Infielder">infielders</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Second_basemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Second basemen">second basemen</a>&#160;(16), <a href="/wiki/Third_basemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Third basemen">third basemen</a>&#160;(15), and <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstops</a>&#160;(15). Of the 25&#160;<a href="/wiki/Pitcher" title="Pitcher">pitchers</a> who have won the award, 15 are <a href="/wiki/Right-handed" class="mw-redirect" title="Right-handed">right-handed</a> while 10 are <a href="/wiki/Left-handed" class="mw-redirect" title="Left-handed">left-handed</a>. <a href="/wiki/Walter_Johnson" title="Walter Johnson">Walter Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Hubbell" title="Carl Hubbell">Carl Hubbell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hal_Newhouser" title="Hal Newhouser">Hal Newhouser</a> are the only pitchers who have won multiple times, Newhouser winning consecutively in 1944 and 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-BD_2000_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BD_2000-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hank_Greenberg" title="Hank Greenberg">Hank Greenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Yount" title="Robin Yount">Robin Yount</a> have won at different positions,<sup id="cite_ref-BD_2000_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BD_2000-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> while Rodriguez is the only player who has won the award with two different teams at two different positions.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds" title="Barry Bonds">Barry Bonds</a> has won the most often&#160;(seven times) and the most consecutively&#160;(four: 2001\xe2\x80\x9304).<sup id="cite_ref-Bonds_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonds-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">Jimmie Foxx</a> was the first player to win multiple times;<sup id="cite_ref-Foxx_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foxx-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> 9&#160;players have won three times, and 19 have won twice.<sup id="cite_ref-winner_list_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winner_list-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a> is the only player to win the award in both the American and National Leagues.\n</p><p>The award\'s only tie occurred in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in 1979, when <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willie_Stargell" title="Willie Stargell">Willie Stargell</a> received an equal number of points.<sup id="cite_ref-BD_2000_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BD_2000-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1979_awards_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1979_awards-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> There have been 18 unanimous winners, who received all the first-place votes.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> have the most winning players with 22, followed by the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> with 17&#160;winners. The award has never been presented to a member of the following three teams: <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a>. The most recent recipients are <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Altuve" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Altuve">Jos\xc3\xa9 Altuve</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giancarlo_Stanton" title="Giancarlo Stanton">Giancarlo Stanton</a> in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>.\n</p><p>In recent decades, pitchers have rarely won the award. When <a href="/wiki/Justin_Verlander" title="Justin Verlander">Justin Verlander</a> won the AL award in 2011, he became the first pitcher in either league to be named the MVP since <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Eckersley" title="Dennis Eckersley">Dennis Eckersley</a> in 1992. Verlander also became the first <a href="/wiki/Starting_pitcher" title="Starting pitcher">starting pitcher</a> to win this award since Roger Clemens accomplished the feat in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The National League went even longer without an MVP award to a pitcher. After <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a> won in 1968, no pitcher in that league was named MVP until <a href="/wiki/Clayton_Kershaw" title="Clayton Kershaw">Clayton Kershaw</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Kershaw_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kershaw-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Chalmers_Award_(1911\xe2\x80\x931914)"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Chalmers Award (1911\xe2\x80\x931914)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#League_Awards_(1922\xe2\x80\x931929)"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">League Awards (1922\xe2\x80\x931929)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Baseball_Writers&#39;_Association_of_America&#39;s_Most_Valuable_Player_(1931\xe2\x80\x93present)"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball Writers\' Association of America\'s Most Valuable Player (1931\xe2\x80\x93present)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Key"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Key</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span id="Chalmers_Award_.281911.E2.80.931914.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Chalmers_Award_(1911\xe2\x80\x931914)">Chalmers Award (1911\xe2\x80\x931914)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Chalmers Award (1911\xe2\x80\x931914)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="Ty Cobb looking just to the left of the camera." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg/220px-Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg" width="220" height="305" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg/330px-Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg/440px-Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1074" data-file-height="1488" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ty-Cobb-1913-NPC-detail-1.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a> won the first American League Chalmers Award in 1911 and was at the center of the controversy over the previous season\'s award.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/1910_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1910 Major League Baseball season">1910 season</a>, Hugh Chalmers of <a href="/wiki/Chalmers_Automobile" title="Chalmers Automobile">Chalmers Automobile</a> announced he would present a Chalmers Model 30 automobile to the player with the highest <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a> in Major League Baseball at the end of the season. The <a href="/wiki/1910_Chalmers_Award" title="1910 Chalmers Award">1910 race for best average in the American League</a> was between the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a>\' widely disliked<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nap_Lajoie" title="Nap Lajoie">Nap Lajoie</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>. On the last day of the season, Lajoie overtook Cobb\'s batting average with seven <a href="/wiki/Bunt_(baseball)" title="Bunt (baseball)">bunt</a> hits against the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Browns" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a>. American League President <a href="/wiki/Ban_Johnson" title="Ban Johnson">Ban Johnson</a> said a recalculation showed that Cobb had won the race anyway, and Chalmers ended up awarding cars to both players.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1911_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1911 Major League Baseball season">following season</a>, Chalmers created the Chalmers Award. A committee of baseball writers were to convene after the season to determine the "most important and useful player to the club and to the league". Since the award was not as effective at advertising as Chalmers had hoped, it was discontinued after 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Year\n</th>\n<th scope="col">American League winner\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Team\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Position\n</th>\n<th scope="col">National League winner\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Team\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Position\n</th>\n<th scope="col" class="unsortable">Ref\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1911_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1911 Major League Baseball season">1911</a>\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center; background:#ffb;"><span data-sort-value="Cobb Ty&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a></span><sup><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></sup><sup>\xc2\xa7</sup>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a></td>\n<td>OF\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center"><span data-sort-value="Schulte Frank&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Frank_Schulte" title="Frank Schulte">Frank Schulte</a></span>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a></td>\n<td>OF</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-1911_awards_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1911_awards-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1912_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1912 Major League Baseball season">1912</a>\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center; background:#ffb;"><span data-sort-value="Speaker Tris&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Tris_Speaker" title="Tris Speaker">Tris Speaker</a></span><sup><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></sup>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a></td>\n<td>OF\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center"><span data-sort-value="Doyle Larry&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Larry_Doyle_(baseball)" title="Larry Doyle (baseball)">Larry Doyle</a></span>\n</th>\n<td><span data-sort-value="New York Giants&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a></span></td>\n<td>2B</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-1912_awards_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1912_awards-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1913_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1913 Major League Baseball season">1913</a>\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center; background:#ffb;"><span data-sort-value="Johnson Walter&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Walter_Johnson" title="Walter Johnson">Walter Johnson</a></span><sup><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></sup>\n</th>\n<td><span data-sort-value="Washington Senators&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1901%E2%80%9360)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)">Washington Senators</a></span></td>\n<td>RHP\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center"><span data-sort-value="Daubert Jake&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Jake_Daubert" title="Jake Daubert">Jake Daubert</a></span>\n</th>\n<td><span data-sort-value="Brooklyn Dodgers&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a></span></td>\n<td>1B</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-1913_awards_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1913_awards-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1914_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1914 Major League Baseball season">1914</a>\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center; background:#ffb;"><span data-sort-value="Collins Eddie&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Eddie_Collins" title="Eddie Collins">Eddie Collins</a></span><sup><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></sup>\n</th>\n<td><span data-sort-value="Philadelphia Athletics&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Athletics">Philadelphia Athletics</a></span></td>\n<td>2B\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center; background:#ffb;"><span data-sort-value="Evers Johnny&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Johnny_Evers" title="Johnny Evers">Johnny Evers</a></span><sup><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></sup>\n</th>\n<td><span data-sort-value="Boston Braves&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Boston_Braves_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Braves (baseball)">Boston Braves</a></span></td>\n<td>2B</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-1914_awards_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1914_awards-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span id="League_Awards_.281922.E2.80.931929.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="League_Awards_(1922\xe2\x80\x931929)">League Awards (1922\xe2\x80\x931929)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: League Awards (1922\xe2\x80\x931929)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Babe_Ruth2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man in full baseball attire wears a pinstriped jersey and a hat with overlapping white &quot;N&quot; and &quot;Y&quot;. Looking to the left of the camera, he is holding a baseball upward." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Babe_Ruth2.jpg/220px-Babe_Ruth2.jpg" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Babe_Ruth2.jpg/330px-Babe_Ruth2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Babe_Ruth2.jpg/440px-Babe_Ruth2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2623" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Babe_Ruth2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> was ineligible for the award in his famous 1927 season by the rules of the American League award because he had previously won in 1923.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1922 the American League created a new award to honor "the baseball player who is of the greatest all-around service to his club".<sup id="cite_ref-A-Rod_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A-Rod-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Winners, voted on by a committee of eight baseball writers chaired by <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_Crusinberry&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James Crusinberry (page does not exist)">James Crusinberry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> received a bronze medal and a cash prize.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Voters were required to select one player from each team and <a href="/wiki/Player-coach" title="Player-coach">player-coaches</a> and prior award winners were ineligible. Famously, these criteria resulted in Babe Ruth winning only a single MVP award before it was dropped after 1928. The National League award, without these restrictions, lasted from 1924 to 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Year\n</th>\n<th scope="col">American League winner\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Team\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Position\n</th>\n<th scope="col">National League winner\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Team\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Position\n</th>\n<th scope="col" class="unsortable">Ref\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1922_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1922 Major League Baseball season">1922</a>\n</td>\n<th scope="row" style="text-align:center; background:#ffb;"><span data-sort-value="Hornsby Rogers&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a></span><sup><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">(2)</span>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a></td>\n<td>2B</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-1929_awards_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1929_awards-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span id="Baseball_Writers.27_Association_of_America.27s_Most_Valuable_Player_.281931.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball_Writers\'_Association_of_America\'s_Most_Valuable_Player_(1931\xe2\x80\x93present)">Baseball Writers\' Association of America\'s Most Valuable Player (1931\xe2\x80\x93present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Baseball Writers&#039; Association of America&#039;s Most Valuable Player (1931\xe2\x80\x93present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The BBWAA first awarded the modern MVP after the <a href="/wiki/1931_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1931 Major League Baseball season">1931 season</a>, adopting the format the National League used to distribute its league award. One writer in each city with a team filled out a ten-place ballot, with ten points for the recipient of a first-place vote, nine for a second-place vote, and so on. In 1938, the BBWAA raised the number of voters to three per city and gave 14 points for a first-place vote. The only significant change since then occurred in 1961, when the number of voters was reduced to two per league city.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man is pictured from his belt up looking to the left of the camera. His button-down baseball jersey says &quot;RED SOX&quot; across it and he is wearing a baseball hat with a &quot;B&quot;." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg/220px-Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg/330px-Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg/440px-Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="812" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jimmie_Foxx_1937_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">Jimmie Foxx</a> was the first player to win three MVP awards.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg/220px-Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg/330px-Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg/440px-Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="674" data-file-height="925" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hank_Greenberg_1937_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hall of Famer and 2-time MVP, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Greenberg" title="Hank Greenberg">Hank Greenberg</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jim_Konstanty.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Jim_Konstanty.jpg/220px-Jim_Konstanty.jpg" width="220" height="351" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a0/Jim_Konstanty.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="245" data-file-height="391" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jim_Konstanty.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jim_Konstanty" title="Jim Konstanty">Jim Konstanty</a>, to date the only National League relief pitcher to href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/This_Year_in_Baseball_Awards#Awards" title="This Year in Baseball Awards">"Esurance MLB Awards"</a> Best Major Leaguer (in MLB; all positions) (there are also Best Hitter and Best Pitcher awards (in MLB))</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Players_Choice_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Players Choice Award">Players Choice Awards</a>" Player of the Year (in MLB; all positions) (there are also Outstanding Player and Outstanding Pitcher awards (in each league))</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baseball_America_Major_League_Player_of_the_Year" title="Baseball America Major League Player of the Year"><i>Baseball America</i> Major League Player of the Year</a> (in MLB; all positions)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Baseball_Digest" title="Baseball Digest">Baseball Digest</a></i> Player of the Year (in MLB; position players only; from 1969 to 1993, included all positions; in 1994, a separate Pitcher of the Year award was added)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Best_Major_League_Baseball_Player_ESPY_Award" title="Best Major League Baseball Player ESPY Award">Best Major League Baseball Player ESPY Award</a> (in MLB; all positions)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="The Sporting News Most Valuable Player Award"><i>The Sporting News</i> Most Valuable Player Award</a> (in each league) (<i>discontinued in 1946</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News_Player_of_the_Year_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sporting News Player of the Year Award"><i>Sporting News</i> Player of the Year</a> (in MLB; position players only)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_awards" title="List of Major League Baseball awards">List of Major League Baseball awards</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baseball_awards#U.S._major_leagues:_Awards_by_organizations_other_than_MLB" title="Baseball awards">Baseball awards</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Numbera"><a href="#ref_Numbera"><b><sup>a</sup></b></a></span>  A player is considered inactive if he has announced his retirement or not played for a full season.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Numberb"><a href="#ref_Numberb"><b><sup>b</sup></b></a></span>  A unanimous victory indicates that the player received all possible first-place votes.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Numberc"><a href="#ref_Numberc"><b><sup>c</sup></b></a></span>  Torre is a member of the Hall of Fame, but not as a player. He was inducted in <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_balloting,_2014" title="Baseball Hall of Fame balloting, 2014">2014</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Manager_(baseball)" title="Manager (baseball)">manager</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Numberd"><a href="#ref_Numberd"><b><sup>d</sup></b></a></span>  Hernandez and Stargell both received 216&#160;points in the 1979 voting.<sup id="cite_ref-1979_awards_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1979_awards-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-LandisNBHoF-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-LandisNBHoF_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-LandisNBHoF_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://baseballhall.org/hof/landis-kenesaw">"Landis, Kenesaw"</a>.
